Such informers, in turn, are key components\n    33→// in the high level controllers that form the backbone of the\n    34→// Kubernetes control plane.  Look at those for examples, or the\n    35→// example in\n    36→// https://github.com/kubernetes/client-go/tree/master/examples/workqueue\n    37→// .\n    38→\n    39→// Config contains all the settings for one of these low-level controllers.\n    40→type Config struct {\n    41→\t// The queue for your objects - has to be a DeltaFIFO due to\n    42→\t// assumptions in the implementation. Your Process() function\n    43→\t// should accept the output of this Queue's Pop() method.\n    44→\tQueue\n    45→\n    46→\t// Something that can list and watch your objects.\n    47→\tListerWatcher\n    48→\n    49→\t// Something that can process a popped Deltas.\n    50→\tProcess ProcessFunc\n    51→\n    52→\t// ObjectType is an example object of the type this controller is\n    53→\t// expected to handle.\n    54→\tObjectType runtime.Object\n    55→\n    56→\t// ObjectDescription is the description to use when logging type-specific information about this controller.\n    57→\tObjectDescription string\n    58→\n    59→\t// FullResyncPeriod is the period at which ShouldResync is considered.\n    60→\tFullResyncPeriod time.Duration\n    61→\n    62→\t// MinWatchTimeout, if set, will define the minimum timeout for watch requests send\n    63→\t// to kube-apiserver. However, values lower than 5m will not be honored to avoid\n    64→\t// negative performance impact on controlplane.\n    65→\t// Optional - if unset a default value of 5m will be used.\n    66→\tMinWatchTimeout time.Duration\n    67→\n    68→\t// ShouldResync is periodically used by the reflector to determine\n    69→\t// whether to Resync the Queue. If ShouldResync is `nil` or\n    70→\t// returns true, it means the reflector should proceed with the\n    71→\t// resync.\n    72→\tShouldResync ShouldResyncFunc\n    73→\n    74→\t// If true, when Process() returns an error, re-enqueue the object.\n    75→\t// TODO: add interface to let you inject a delay/backoff or drop\n    76→\t//       the object completely if desired. Pass the object in\n    77→\t//       question to this interface as a parameter.  This is probably moot\n    78→\t//       now that this functionality appears at a higher level.\n    79→\tRetryOnError bool\n    80→\n    81→\t// Called whenever the ListAndWatch drops the connection with an error.\n    82→\tWatchErrorHandler WatchErrorHandler\n    83→\n    84→\t// WatchListPageSize is the requested chunk size of initial and relist watch lists.\n    85→\tWatchListPageSize int64\n    86→}\n    87→\n    88→// ShouldResyncFunc is a type of function that indicates if a reflector should perform a\n    89→// resync or not. It can be used by a shared informer to support multiple event handlers with custom\n    90→// resync periods.\n    91→type ShouldResyncFunc func() bool\n    92→\n    93→// ProcessFunc processes a single object.\n    94→type ProcessFunc func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) error\n    95→\n    96→// `*controller` implements Controller\n    97→type controller struct {\n    98→\tconfig         Config\n    99→\treflector      *Reflector\n   100→\treflectorMutex sync.RWMutex\n   101→\tclock          clock.Clock\n   102→}\n   103→\n   104→// Controller is a low-level controller that is parameterized by a\n   105→// Config and used in sharedIndexInformer.\n   106→type Controller interface {\n   107→\t// Run does two things.  One is to construct and run a Reflector\n   108→\t// to pump objects/notifications from the Config's ListerWatcher\n   109→\t// to the Config's Queue and possibly invoke the occasional Resync\n   110→\t// on that Queue.  The other is to repeatedly Pop from the Queue\n   111→\t// and process with the Config's ProcessFunc.  Both of these\n   112→\t// continue until `stopCh` is closed.\n   113→\tRun(stopCh <-chan struct{})\n   114→\n   115→\t// HasSynced delegates to the Config's Queue\n   116→\tHasSynced() bool\n   117→\n   118→\t// LastSyncResourceVersion delegates to the Reflector when there\n   119→\t// is one, otherwise returns the empty string\n   120→\tLastSyncResourceVersion() string\n   121→}\n   122→\n   123→// New makes a new Controller from the given Config.\n   124→func New(c *Config) Controller {\n   125→\tctlr := &controller{\n   126→\t\tconfig: *c,\n   127→\t\tclock:  &clock.RealClock{},\n   128→\t}\n   129→\treturn ctlr\n   130→}\n   131→\n   132→// Run begins processing items, and will continue until a value is sent down stopCh or it is closed.\n   133→// It's an error to call Run more than once.\n   134→// Run blocks; call via go.\n   135→func (c *controller) Run(stopCh <-chan struct{}) {\n   136→\tdefer utilruntime.HandleCrash()\n   137→\tgo func() {\n   138→\t\t<-stopCh\n   139→\t\tc.config.Queue.Close()\n   140→\t}()\n   141→\tr := NewReflectorWithOptions(\n   142→\t\tc.config.ListerWatcher,\n   143→\t\tc.config.ObjectType,\n   144→\t\tc.config.Queue,\n   145→\t\tReflectorOptions{\n   146→\t\t\tResyncPeriod:    c.config.FullResyncPeriod,\n   147→\t\t\tMinWatchTimeout: c.config.MinWatchTimeout,\n   148→\t\t\tTypeDescription: c.config.ObjectDescription,\n   149→\t\t\tClock:           c.clock,\n   150→\t\t},\n   151→\t)\n   152→\tr.ShouldResync = c.config.ShouldResync\n   153→\tr.WatchListPageSize = c.config.WatchListPageSize\n   154→\tif c.config.WatchErrorHandler != nil {\n   155→\t\tr.watchErrorHandler = c.config.WatchErrorHandler\n   156→\t}\n   157→\n   158→\tc.reflectorMutex.Lock()\n   159→\tc.reflector = r\n   160→\tc.reflectorMutex.Unlock()\n   161→\n   162→\tvar wg wait.Group\n   163→\n   164→\twg.StartWithChannel(stopCh, r.Run)\n   165→\n   166→\twait.Until(c.processLoop, time.Second, stopCh)\n   167→\twg.Wait()\n   168→}\n   169→\n   170→// Returns true once this controller has completed an initial resource listing\n   171→func (c *controller) HasSynced() bool {\n   172→\treturn c.config.Queue.HasSynced()\n   173→}\n   174→\n   175→func (c *controller) LastSyncResourceVersion() string {\n   176→\tc.reflectorMutex.RLock()\n   177→\tdefer c.reflectorMutex.RUnlock()\n   178→\tif c.reflector == nil {\n   179→\t\treturn \"\"\n   180→\t}\n   181→\treturn c.reflector.LastSyncResourceVersion()\n   182→}\n   183→\n   184→// processLoop drains the work queue.\n   185→// TODO: Consider doing the processing in parallel. This will require a little thought\n   186→// to make sure that we don't end up processing the same object multiple times\n   187→// concurrently.\n   188→//\n   189→// TODO: Plumb through the stopCh here (and down to the queue) so that this can\n   190→// actually exit when the controller is stopped. Or just give up on this stuff\n   191→// ever being stoppable. Converting this whole package to use Context would\n   192→// also be helpful.\n   193→func (c *controller) processLoop() {\n   194→\tfor {\n   195→\t\tobj, err := c.config.Queue.Pop(PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))\n   196→\t\tif err != nil {\n   197→\t\t\tif err == ErrFIFOClosed {\n   198→\t\t\t\treturn\n   199→\t\t\t}\n   200→\t\t\tif c.config.RetryOnError {\n   201→\t\t\t\t// This is the safe way to re-enqueue.\n   202→\t\t\t\tc.config.Queue.AddIfNotPresent(obj)\n   203→\t\t\t}\n   204→\t\t}\n   205→\t}\n   206→}\n   207→\n   208→// ResourceEventHandler can handle notifications for events that\n   209→// happen to a resource. The events are informational only, so you\n   210→// can't return an error.  The handlers MUST NOT modify the objects\n   211→// received; this concerns not only the top level of structure but all\n   212→// the data structures reachable from it.\n   213→//   - OnAdd is called when an object is added.\n   214→//   - OnUpdate is called when an object is modified. Note that oldObj is the\n   215→//     last known state of the object-- it is possible that several changes\n   216→//     were combined together, so you can't use this to see every single\n   217→//     change. OnUpdate is also called when a re-list happens, and it will\n   218→//     get called even if nothing changed. This is useful for periodically\n   219→//     evaluating or syncing something.\n   220→//   - OnDelete will get the final state of the item if it is known, otherwise\n   221→//     it will get an object of type DeletedFinalStateUnknown. This can\n   222→//     happen if the watch is closed and misses the delete event and we don't\n   223→//     notice the deletion until the subsequent re-list.\n   224→type ResourceEventHandler interface {\n   225→\tOnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool)\n   226→\tOnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n   227→\tOnDelete(obj interface{})\n   228→}\n   229→\n   230→// ResourceEventHandlerFuncs is an adaptor to let you easily specify as many or\n   231→// as few of the notification functions as you want while still implementing\n   232→// ResourceEventHandler.  This adapter does not remove the prohibition against\n   233→// modifying the objects.\n   234→//\n   235→// See ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs if your use needs to propagate\n   236→// HasSynced.\n   237→type ResourceEventHandlerFuncs struct {\n   238→\tAddFunc    func(obj interface{})\n   239→\tUpdateFunc func(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n   240→\tDeleteFunc func(obj interface{})\n   241→}\n   242→\n   243→// OnAdd calls AddFunc if it's not nil.\n   244→func (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n   245→\tif r.AddFunc != nil {\n   246→\t\tr.AddFunc(obj)\n   247→\t}\n   248→}\n   249→\n   250→// OnUpdate calls UpdateFunc if it's not nil.\n   251→func (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n   252→\tif r.UpdateFunc != nil {\n   253→\t\tr.UpdateFunc(oldObj, newObj)\n   254→\t}\n   255→}\n   256→\n   257→// OnDelete calls DeleteFunc if it's not nil.\n   258→func (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n   259→\tif r.DeleteFunc != nil {\n   260→\t\tr.DeleteFunc(obj)\n   261→\t}\n   262→}\n   263→\n   264→// ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs is exactly like ResourceEventHandlerFuncs\n   265→// except its AddFunc accepts the isInInitialList parameter, for propagating\n   266→// HasSynced.\n   267→type ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs struct {\n   268→\tAddFunc    func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool)\n   269→\tUpdateFunc func(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n   270→\tDeleteFunc func(obj interface{})\n   271→}\n   272→\n   273→// OnAdd calls AddFunc if it's not nil.\n   274→func (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n   275→\tif r.AddFunc != nil {\n   276→\t\tr.AddFunc(obj, isInInitialList)\n   277→\t}\n   278→}\n   279→\n   280→// OnUpdate calls UpdateFunc if it's not nil.\n   281→func (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n   282→\tif r.UpdateFunc != nil {\n   283→\t\tr.UpdateFunc(oldObj, newObj)\n   284→\t}\n   285→}\n   286→\n   287→// OnDelete calls DeleteFunc if it's not nil.\n   288→func (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n   289→\tif r.DeleteFunc != nil {\n   290→\t\tr.DeleteFunc(obj)\n   291→\t}\n   292→}\n   293→\n   294→// FilteringResourceEventHandler applies the provided filter to all events coming\n   295→// in, ensuring the appropriate nested handler method is invoked. An object\n   296→// that starts passing the filter after an update is considered an add, and an\n   297→// object that stops passing the filter after an update is considered a delete.\n   298→// Like the handlers, the filter MUST NOT modify the objects it is given.\n   299→type FilteringResourceEventHandler struct {\n   300→\tFilterFunc func(obj interface{}) bool\n   301→\tHandler    ResourceEventHandler\n   302→}\n   303→\n   304→// OnAdd calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\n   305→func (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n   306→\tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\n   307→\t\treturn\n   308→\t}\n   309→\tr.Handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n   310→}\n   311→\n   312→// OnUpdate ensures the proper handler is called depending on whether the filter matches\n   313→func (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n   314→\tnewer := r.FilterFunc(newObj)\n   315→\tolder := r.FilterFunc(oldObj)\n   316→\tswitch {\n   317→\tcase newer && older:\n   318→\t\tr.Handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj)\n   319→\tcase newer && !older:\n   320→\t\tr.Handler.OnAdd(newObj, false)\n   321→\tcase !newer && older:\n   322→\t\tr.Handler.OnDelete(oldObj)\n   323→\tdefault:\n   324→\t\t// do nothing\n   325→\t}\n   326→}\n   327→\n   328→// OnDelete calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\n   329→func (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n   330→\tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\n   331→\t\treturn\n   332→\t}\n   333→\tr.Handler.OnDelete(obj)\n   334→}\n   335→\n   336→// DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc checks for\n   337→// DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\n   338→// MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\n   339→func DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj interface{}) (string, error) {\n   340→\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\n   341→\t\treturn d.Key, nil\n   342→\t}\n   343→\treturn MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n   344→}\n   345→\n   346→// DeletionHandlingObjectToName checks for\n   347→// DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\n   348→// ObjectToName.\n   349→func DeletionHandlingObjectToName(obj interface{}) (ObjectName, error) {\n   350→\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\n   351→\t\treturn ParseObjectName(d.Key)\n   352→\t}\n   353→\treturn ObjectToName(obj)\n   354→}\n   355→\n   356→// InformerOptions configure a Reflector.\n   357→type InformerOptions struct {\n   358→\t// ListerWatcher implements List and Watch functions for the source of the resource\n   359→\t// the informer will be informing about.\n   360→\tListerWatcher ListerWatcher\n   361→\n   362→\t// ObjectType is an object of the type that informer is expected to receive.\n   363→\tObjectType runtime.Object\n   364→\n   365→\t// Handler defines functions that should called on object mutations.\n   366→\tHandler ResourceEventHandler\n   367→\n   368→\t// ResyncPeriod is the underlying Reflector's resync period. If non-zero, the store\n   369→\t// is re-synced with that frequency - Modify events are delivered even if objects\n   370→\t// didn't change.\n   371→\t// This is useful for synchronizing objects that configure external resources\n   372→\t// (e.g. configure cloud provider functionalities).\n   373→\t// Optional - if unset, store resyncing is not happening periodically.\n   374→\tResyncPeriod time.Duration\n   375→\n   376→\t// MinWatchTimeout, if set, will define the minimum timeout for watch requests send\n   377→\t// to kube-apiserver. However, values lower than 5m will not be honored to avoid\n   378→\t// negative performance impact on controlplane.\n   379→\t// Optional - if unset a default value of 5m will be used.\n   380→\tMinWatchTimeout time.Duration\n   381→\n   382→\t// Indexers, if set, are the indexers for the received objects to optimize\n   383→\t// certain queries.\n   384→\t// Optional - if unset no indexes are maintained.\n   385→\tIndexers Indexers\n   386→\n   387→\t// Transform function, if set, will be called on all objects before they will be\n   388→\t// put into the Store and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will be invoked\n   389→\t// for them.\n   390→\t// Optional - if unset no additional transforming is happening.\n   391→\tTransform TransformFunc\n   392→}\n   393→\n   394→// NewInformerWithOptions returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\n   395→// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n   396→// Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n   397→// notifications to be faulty.\n   398→func NewInformerWithOptions(options InformerOptions) (Store, Controller) {\n   399→\tvar clientState Store\n   400→\tif options.Indexers == nil {\n   401→\t\tclientState = NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n   402→\t} else {\n   403→\t\tclientState = NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, options.Indexers)\n   404→\t}\n   405→\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options)\n   406→}\n   407→\n   408→// NewInformer returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\n   409→// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n   410→// Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n   411→// notifications to be faulty.\n   412→//\n   413→// Parameters:\n   414→//   - lw is list and watch functions for the source of the resource you want to\n   415→//     be informed of.\n   416→//   - objType is an object of the type that you expect to receive.\n   417→//   - resyncPeriod: if non-zero, will re-list this often (you will get OnUpdate\n   418→//     calls, even if nothing changed). Otherwise, re-list will be delayed as\n   419→//     long as possible (until the upstream source closes the watch or times out,\n   420→//     or you stop the controller).\n   421→//   - h is the object you want notifications sent to.\n   422→//\n   423→// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\n   424→func NewInformer(\n   425→\tlw ListerWatcher,\n   426→\tobjType runtime.Object,\n   427→\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n   428→\th ResourceEventHandler,\n   429→) (Store, Controller) {\n   430→\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n   431→\tclientState := NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n   432→\n   433→\toptions := InformerOptions{\n   434→\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n   435→\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n   436→\t\tHandler:       h,\n   437→\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n   438→\t}\n   439→\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options)\n   440→}\n   441→\n   442→// NewIndexerInformer returns an Indexer and a Controller for populating the index\n   443→// while also providing event notifications. You should\n   510→// only used the returned Index for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes\n   511→// will cause the event notifications to be faulty.\n   512→// The given transform function will be called on all objects before they will\n   513→// be put into the Index and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will\n   514→// be invoked for them.\n   515→//\n   516→// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\n   517→func NewTransformingIndexerInformer(\n   518→\tlw ListerWatcher,\n   519→\tobjType runtime.Object,\n   520→\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n   521→\th ResourceEventHandler,\n   522→\tindexers Indexers,\n   523→\ttransformer TransformFunc,\n   524→) (Indexer, Controller) {\n   525→\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n   526→\tclientState := NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, indexers)\n   527→\n   528→\toptions := InformerOptions{\n   529→\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n   530→\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n   531→\t\tHandler:       h,\n   532→\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n   533→\t\tIndexers:      indexers,\n   534→\t\tTransform:     transformer,\n   535→\t}\n   536→\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options)\n   537→}\n   538→\n   539→// Multiplexes updates in the form of a list of Deltas into a Store, and informs\n   540→// a given handler of events OnUpdate, OnAdd, OnDelete\n   541→func processDeltas(\n   542→\t// Object which receives event notifications from the given deltas\n   543→\thandler ResourceEventHandler,\n   544→\tclientState Store,\n   545→\tdeltas Deltas,\n   546→\tisInInitialList bool,\n   547→) error {\n   548→\t// from oldest to newest\n   549→\tfor _, d := range deltas {\n   550→\t\tobj := d.Object\n   551→\n   552→\t\tswitch d.Type {\n   553→\t\tcase Sync, Replaced, Added, Updated:\n   554→\t\t\tif old, exists, err := clientState.Get(obj); err == nil && exists {\n   555→\t\t\t\tif err := clientState.Update(obj); err != nil {\n   556→\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n   557→\t\t\t\t}\n   558→\t\t\t\thandler.OnUpdate(old, obj)\n   559→\t\t\t} else {\n   560→\t\t\t\tif err := clientState.Add(obj); err != nil {\n   561→\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n   562→\t\t\t\t}\n   563→\t\t\t\thandler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n   564→\t\t\t}\n   565→\t\tcase Deleted:\n   566→\t\t\tif err := clientState.Delete(obj); err != nil {\n   567→\t\t\t\treturn err\n   568→\t\t\t}\n   569→\t\t\thandler.OnDelete(obj)\n   570→\t\t}\n   571→\t}\n   572→\treturn nil\n   573→}\n   574→\n   575→// newInformer returns a controller for populating the store while also\n   576→// providing event notifications.\n   577→//\n   578→// Parameters\n   579→//   - clientState is the store you want to populate\n   580→//   - options contain the options to configure the controller\n   581→func newInformer(clientState Store, options InformerOptions) Controller {\n   582→\t// This will hold incoming changes. Note how we pass clientState in as a\n   583→\t// KeyLister, that way resync operations will result in the correct set\n   584→\t// of update/delete deltas.\n   585→\tfifo := NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{\n   586→\t\tKnownObjects:          clientState,\n   587→\t\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced: true,\n   588→\t\tTransformer:           options.Transform,\n   589→\t})\n   590→\n   591→\tcfg := &Config{\n   592→\t\tQueue:            fifo,\n   593→\t\tListerWatcher:    options.ListerWatcher,\n   594→\t\tObjectType:       options.ObjectType,\n   595→\t\tFullResyncPeriod: options.ResyncPeriod,\n   596→\t\tMinWatchTimeout:  options.MinWatchTimeout,\n   597→\t\tRetryOnError:     false,\n   598→\n   599→\t\tProcess: func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) error {\n   600→\t\t\tif deltas, ok := obj.(Deltas); ok {\n   601→\t\t\t\treturn processDeltas(options.Handler, clientState, deltas, isInInitialList)\n   602→\t\t\t}\n   603→\t\t\treturn errors.New(\"object given as Process argument is not Deltas\")\n   604→\t\t},\n   605→\t}\n   606→\treturn New(cfg)\n   607→}\n   608→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Such informers, in turn, are key components\n// in the high level controllers that form the backbone of the\n// Kubernetes control plane.  Look at those for examples, or the\n// example in\n// https://github.com/kubernetes/client-go/tree/master/examples/workqueue\n// .\n\n// Config contains all the settings for one of these low-level controllers.\ntype Config struct {\n\t// The queue for your objects - has to be a DeltaFIFO due to\n\t// assumptions in the implementation. Your Process() function\n\t// should accept the output of this Queue's Pop() method.\n\tQueue\n\n\t// Something that can list and watch your objects.\n\tListerWatcher\n\n\t// Something that can process a popped Deltas.\n\tProcess ProcessFunc\n\n\t// ObjectType is an example object of the type this controller is\n\t// expected to handle.\n\tObjectType runtime.Object\n\n\t// ObjectDescription is the description to use when logging type-specific information about this controller.\n\tObjectDescription string\n\n\t// FullResyncPeriod is the period at which ShouldResync is considered.\n\tFullResyncPeriod time.Duration\n\n\t// MinWatchTimeout, if set, will define the minimum timeout for watch requests send\n\t// to kube-apiserver. However, values lower than 5m will not be honored to avoid\n\t// negative performance impact on controlplane.\n\t// Optional - if unset a default value of 5m will be used.\n\tMinWatchTimeout time.Duration\n\n\t// ShouldResync is periodically used by the reflector to determine\n\t// whether to Resync the Queue. If ShouldResync is `nil` or\n\t// returns true, it means the reflector should proceed with the\n\t// resync.\n\tShouldResync ShouldResyncFunc\n\n\t// If true, when Process() returns an error, re-enqueue the object.\n\t// TODO: add interface to let you inject a delay/backoff or drop\n\t//       the object completely if desired. Pass the object in\n\t//       question to this interface as a parameter.  This is probably moot\n\t//       now that this functionality appears at a higher level.\n\tRetryOnError bool\n\n\t// Called whenever the ListAndWatch drops the connection with an error.\n\tWatchErrorHandler WatchErrorHandler\n\n\t// WatchListPageSize is the requested chunk size of initial and relist watch lists.\n\tWatchListPageSize int64\n}\n\n// ShouldResyncFunc is a type of function that indicates if a reflector should perform a\n// resync or not. It can be used by a shared informer to support multiple event handlers with custom\n// resync periods.\ntype ShouldResyncFunc func() bool\n\n// ProcessFunc processes a single object.\ntype ProcessFunc func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) error\n\n// `*controller` implements Controller\ntype controller struct {\n\tconfig         Config\n\treflector      *Reflector\n\treflectorMutex sync.RWMutex\n\tclock          clock.Clock\n}\n\n// Controller is a low-level controller that is parameterized by a\n// Config and used in sharedIndexInformer.\ntype Controller interface {\n\t// Run does two things.  One is to construct and run a Reflector\n\t// to pump objects/notifications from the Config's ListerWatcher\n\t// to the Config's Queue and possibly invoke the occasional Resync\n\t// on that Queue.  The other is to repeatedly Pop from the Queue\n\t// and process with the Config's ProcessFunc.  Both of these\n\t// continue until `stopCh` is closed.\n\tRun(stopCh <-chan struct{})\n\n\t// HasSynced delegates to the Config's Queue\n\tHasSynced() bool\n\n\t// LastSyncResourceVersion delegates to the Reflector when there\n\t// is one, otherwise returns the empty string\n\tLastSyncResourceVersion() string\n}\n\n// New makes a new Controller from the given Config.\nfunc New(c *Config) Controller {\n\tctlr := &controller{\n\t\tconfig: *c,\n\t\tclock:  &clock.RealClock{},\n\t}\n\treturn ctlr\n}\n\n// Run begins processing items, and will continue until a value is sent down stopCh or it is closed.\n// It's an error to call Run more than once.\n// Run blocks; call via go.\nfunc (c *controller) Run(stopCh <-chan struct{}) {\n\tdefer utilruntime.HandleCrash()\n\tgo func() {\n\t\t<-stopCh\n\t\tc.config.Queue.Close()\n\t}()\n\tr := NewReflectorWithOptions(\n\t\tc.config.ListerWatcher,\n\t\tc.config.ObjectType,\n\t\tc.config.Queue,\n\t\tReflectorOptions{\n\t\t\tResyncPeriod:    c.config.FullResyncPeriod,\n\t\t\tMinWatchTimeout: c.config.MinWatchTimeout,\n\t\t\tTypeDescription: c.config.ObjectDescription,\n\t\t\tClock:           c.clock,\n\t\t},\n\t)\n\tr.ShouldResync = c.config.ShouldResync\n\tr.WatchListPageSize = c.config.WatchListPageSize\n\tif c.config.WatchErrorHandler != nil {\n\t\tr.watchErrorHandler = c.config.WatchErrorHandler\n\t}\n\n\tc.reflectorMutex.Lock()\n\tc.reflector = r\n\tc.reflectorMutex.Unlock()\n\n\tvar wg wait.Group\n\n\twg.StartWithChannel(stopCh, r.Run)\n\n\twait.Until(c.processLoop, time.Second, stopCh)\n\twg.Wait()\n}\n\n// Returns true once this controller has completed an initial resource listing\nfunc (c *controller) HasSynced() bool {\n\treturn c.config.Queue.HasSynced()\n}\n\nfunc (c *controller) LastSyncResourceVersion() string {\n\tc.reflectorMutex.RLock()\n\tdefer c.reflectorMutex.RUnlock()\n\tif c.reflector == nil {\n\t\treturn \"\"\n\t}\n\treturn c.reflector.LastSyncResourceVersion()\n}\n\n// processLoop drains the work queue.\n// TODO: Consider doing the processing in parallel. This will require a little thought\n// to make sure that we don't end up processing the same object multiple times\n// concurrently.\n//\n// TODO: Plumb through the stopCh here (and down to the queue) so that this can\n// actually exit when the controller is stopped. Or just give up on this stuff\n// ever being stoppable. Converting this whole package to use Context would\n// also be helpful.\nfunc (c *controller) processLoop() {\n\tfor {\n\t\tobj, err := c.config.Queue.Pop(PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tif err == ErrFIFOClosed {\n\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif c.config.RetryOnError {\n\t\t\t\t// This is the safe way to re-enqueue.\n\t\t\t\tc.config.Queue.AddIfNotPresent(obj)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// ResourceEventHandler can handle notifications for events that\n// happen to a resource. The events are informational only, so you\n// can't return an error.  The handlers MUST NOT modify the objects\n// received; this concerns not only the top level of structure but all\n// the data structures reachable from it.\n//   - OnAdd is called when an object is added.\n//   - OnUpdate is called when an object is modified. Note that oldObj is the\n//     last known state of the object-- it is possible that several changes\n//     were combined together, so you can't use this to see every single\n//     change. OnUpdate is also called when a re-list happens, and it will\n//     get called even if nothing changed. This is useful for periodically\n//     evaluating or syncing something.\n//   - OnDelete will get the final state of the item if it is known, otherwise\n//     it will get an object of type DeletedFinalStateUnknown. This can\n//     happen if the watch is closed and misses the delete event and we don't\n//     notice the deletion until the subsequent re-list.\ntype ResourceEventHandler interface {\n\tOnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool)\n\tOnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n\tOnDelete(obj interface{})\n}\n\n// ResourceEventHandlerFuncs is an adaptor to let you easily specify as many or\n// as few of the notification functions as you want while still implementing\n// ResourceEventHandler.  This adapter does not remove the prohibition against\n// modifying the objects.\n//\n// See ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs if your use needs to propagate\n// HasSynced.\ntype ResourceEventHandlerFuncs struct {\n\tAddFunc    func(obj interface{})\n\tUpdateFunc func(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n\tDeleteFunc func(obj interface{})\n}\n\n// OnAdd calls AddFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n\tif r.AddFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.AddFunc(obj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnUpdate calls UpdateFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n\tif r.UpdateFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.UpdateFunc(oldObj, newObj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnDelete calls DeleteFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n\tif r.DeleteFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.DeleteFunc(obj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs is exactly like ResourceEventHandlerFuncs\n// except its AddFunc accepts the isInInitialList parameter, for propagating\n// HasSynced.\ntype ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs struct {\n\tAddFunc    func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool)\n\tUpdateFunc func(oldObj, newObj interface{})\n\tDeleteFunc func(obj interface{})\n}\n\n// OnAdd calls AddFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n\tif r.AddFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.AddFunc(obj, isInInitialList)\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnUpdate calls UpdateFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n\tif r.UpdateFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.UpdateFunc(oldObj, newObj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnDelete calls DeleteFunc if it's not nil.\nfunc (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n\tif r.DeleteFunc != nil {\n\t\tr.DeleteFunc(obj)\n\t}\n}\n\n// FilteringResourceEventHandler applies the provided filter to all events coming\n// in, ensuring the appropriate nested handler method is invoked. An object\n// that starts passing the filter after an update is considered an add, and an\n// object that stops passing the filter after an update is considered a delete.\n// Like the handlers, the filter MUST NOT modify the objects it is given.\ntype FilteringResourceEventHandler struct {\n\tFilterFunc func(obj interface{}) bool\n\tHandler    ResourceEventHandler\n}\n\n// OnAdd calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\nfunc (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\n\tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tr.Handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n}\n\n// OnUpdate ensures the proper handler is called depending on whether the filter matches\nfunc (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\n\tnewer := r.FilterFunc(newObj)\n\tolder := r.FilterFunc(oldObj)\n\tswitch {\n\tcase newer && older:\n\t\tr.Handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj)\n\tcase newer && !older:\n\t\tr.Handler.OnAdd(newObj, false)\n\tcase !newer && older:\n\t\tr.Handler.OnDelete(oldObj)\n\tdefault:\n\t\t// do nothing\n\t}\n}\n\n// OnDelete calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\nfunc (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\n\tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tr.Handler.OnDelete(obj)\n}\n\n// DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc checks for\n// DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\n// MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\nfunc DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj interface{}) (string, error) {\n\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\n\t\treturn d.Key, nil\n\t}\n\treturn MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\n}\n\n// DeletionHandlingObjectToName checks for\n// DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\n// ObjectToName.\nfunc DeletionHandlingObjectToName(obj interface{}) (ObjectName, error) {\n\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\n\t\treturn ParseObjectName(d.Key)\n\t}\n\treturn ObjectToName(obj)\n}\n\n// InformerOptions configure a Reflector.\ntype InformerOptions struct {\n\t// ListerWatcher implements List and Watch functions for the source of the resource\n\t// the informer will be informing about.\n\tListerWatcher ListerWatcher\n\n\t// ObjectType is an object of the type that informer is expected to receive.\n\tObjectType runtime.Object\n\n\t// Handler defines functions that should called on object mutations.\n\tHandler ResourceEventHandler\n\n\t// ResyncPeriod is the underlying Reflector's resync period. If non-zero, the store\n\t// is re-synced with that frequency - Modify events are delivered even if objects\n\t// didn't change.\n\t// This is useful for synchronizing objects that configure external resources\n\t// (e.g. configure cloud provider functionalities).\n\t// Optional - if unset, store resyncing is not happening periodically.\n\tResyncPeriod time.Duration\n\n\t// MinWatchTimeout, if set, will define the minimum timeout for watch requests send\n\t// to kube-apiserver. However, values lower than 5m will not be honored to avoid\n\t// negative performance impact on controlplane.\n\t// Optional - if unset a default value of 5m will be used.\n\tMinWatchTimeout time.Duration\n\n\t// Indexers, if set, are the indexers for the received objects to optimize\n\t// certain queries.\n\t// Optional - if unset no indexes are maintained.\n\tIndexers Indexers\n\n\t// Transform function, if set, will be called on all objects before they will be\n\t// put into the Store and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will be invoked\n\t// for them.\n\t// Optional - if unset no additional transforming is happening.\n\tTransform TransformFunc\n}\n\n// NewInformerWithOptions returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\n// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n// Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n// notifications to be faulty.\nfunc NewInformerWithOptions(options InformerOptions) (Store, Controller) {\n\tvar clientState Store\n\tif options.Indexers == nil {\n\t\tclientState = NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n\t} else {\n\t\tclientState = NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, options.Indexers)\n\t}\n\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options)\n}\n\n// NewInformer returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\n// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n// Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n// notifications to be faulty.\n//\n// Parameters:\n//   - lw is list and watch functions for the source of the resource you want to\n//     be informed of.\n//   - objType is an object of the type that you expect to receive.\n//   - resyncPeriod: if non-zero, will re-list this often (you will get OnUpdate\n//     calls, even if nothing changed). Otherwise, re-list will be delayed as\n//     long as possible (until the upstream source closes the watch or times out,\n//     or you stop the controller).\n//   - h is the object you want notifications sent to.\n//\n// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\nfunc NewInformer(\n\tlw ListerWatcher,\n\tobjType runtime.Object,\n\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n\th ResourceEventHandler,\n) (Store, Controller) {\n\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n\tclientState := NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n\n\toptions := InformerOptions{\n\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n\t\tHandler:       h,\n\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n\t}\n\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options)\n}\n\n// NewIndexerInformer returns an Indexer and a Controller for populating the index\n// while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\n// Index for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\n// notifications to be faulty.\n//\n// Parameters:\n//   - lw is list and watch functions for the source of the resource you want to\n//     be informed of.\n//   - objType is an object of the type that you expect to receive.\n//   - resyncPeriod: if non-zero, will re-list this often (you will get OnUpdate\n//     calls, even if nothing changed). Otherwise, re-list will be delayed as\n//     long as possible (until the upstream source closes the watch or times out,\n//     or you stop the controller).\n//   - h is the object you want notifications sent to.\n//   - indexers is the indexer for the received object type.\n//\n// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\nfunc NewIndexerInformer(\n\tlw ListerWatcher,\n\tobjType runtime.Object,\n\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n\th ResourceEventHandler,\n\tindexers Indexers,\n) (Indexer, Controller) {\n\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n\tclientState := NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, indexers)\n\n\toptions := InformerOptions{\n\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n\t\tHandler:       h,\n\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n\t\tIndexers:      indexers,\n\t}\n\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options)\n}\n\n// NewTransformingInformer returns a Store and a controller for populating\n// the store while also providing event notifications. You should only used\n// the returned Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause\n// the event notifications to be faulty.\n// The given transform function will be called on all objects before they will\n// put into the Store and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will\n// be invoked for them.\n//\n// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\nfunc NewTransformingInformer(\n\tlw ListerWatcher,\n\tobjType runtime.Object,\n\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n\th ResourceEventHandler,\n\ttransformer TransformFunc,\n) (Store, Controller) {\n\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n\tclientState := NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\n\n\toptions := InformerOptions{\n\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n\t\tHandler:       h,\n\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n\t\tTransform:     transformer,\n\t}\n\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options)\n}\n\n// NewTransformingIndexerInformer returns an Indexer and a controller for\n// populating the index while also providing event notifications. You should\n// only used the returned Index for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes\n// will cause the event notifications to be faulty.\n// The given transform function will be called on all objects before they will\n// be put into the Index and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will\n// be invoked for them.\n//\n// Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\nfunc NewTransformingIndexerInformer(\n\tlw ListerWatcher,\n\tobjType runtime.Object,\n\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\n\th ResourceEventHandler,\n\tindexers Indexers,\n\ttransformer TransformFunc,\n) (Indexer, Controller) {\n\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\n\tclientState := NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, indexers)\n\n\toptions := InformerOptions{\n\t\tListerWatcher: lw,\n\t\tObjectType:    objType,\n\t\tHandler:       h,\n\t\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\n\t\tIndexers:      indexers,\n\t\tTransform:     transformer,\n\t}\n\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options)\n}\n\n// Multiplexes updates in the form of a list of Deltas into a Store, and informs\n// a given handler of events OnUpdate, OnAdd, OnDelete\nfunc processDeltas(\n\t// Object which receives event notifications from the given deltas\n\thandler ResourceEventHandler,\n\tclientState Store,\n\tdeltas Deltas,\n\tisInInitialList bool,\n) error {\n\t// from oldest to newest\n\tfor _, d := range deltas {\n\t\tobj := d.Object\n\n\t\tswitch d.Type {\n\t\tcase Sync, Replaced, Added, Updated:\n\t\t\tif old, exists, err := clientState.Get(obj); err == nil && exists {\n\t\t\t\tif err := clientState.Update(obj); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\thandler.OnUpdate(old, obj)\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tif err := clientState.Add(obj); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\thandler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase Deleted:\n\t\t\tif err := clientState.Delete(obj); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\thandler.OnDelete(obj)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// newInformer returns a controller for populating the store while also\n// providing event notifications.\n//\n// Parameters\n//   - clientState is the store you want to populate\n//   - options contain the options to configure the controller\nfunc newInformer(clientState Store, options InformerOptions) Controller {\n\t// This will hold incoming changes. Note how we pass clientState in as a\n\t// KeyLister, that way resync operations will result in the correct set\n\t// of update/delete deltas.\n\tfifo := NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{\n\t\tKnownObjects:          clientState,\n\t\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced: true,\n\t\tTransformer:           options.Transform,\n\t})\n\n\tcfg := &Config{\n\t\tQueue:            fifo,\n\t\tListerWatcher:    options.ListerWatcher,\n\t\tObjectType:       options.ObjectType,\n\t\tFullResyncPeriod: options.ResyncPeriod,\n\t\tMinWatchTimeout:  options.MinWatchTimeout,\n\t\tRetryOnError:     false,\n\n\t\tProcess: func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) error {\n\t\t\tif deltas, ok := obj.(Deltas); ok {\n\t\t\t\treturn processDeltas(options.Handler, clientState, deltas, isInInitialList)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn errors.New(\"object given as Process argument is not Deltas\")\n\t\t},\n\t}\n\treturn New(cfg)\n}\n","numLines":608,"startLine":1,"totalLines":608}}}

An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n    41→// namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n    42→// an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n    43→// SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n    44→// group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n    45→// SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n    46→// applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n    47→//\n    48→// The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n    49→// access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n    50→// An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n    51→// other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n    52→//\n    53→// A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n    54→// by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n    55→// machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n    56→// the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n    57→// consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n    58→// prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n    59→// particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n    60→// then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n    61→// eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n    62→// state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n    63→// service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n    64→// absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n    65→// selector.\n    66→//\n    67→// For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n    68→// states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n    69→// states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n    70→// might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n    71→// states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n    72→// ordering between states seen for different objects.\n    73→//\n    74→// The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n    75→// during `Run()`.\n    76→//\n    77→// As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n    78→// unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n    79→// collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n    80→// SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n    81→// collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n    82→// service ends, or communication problems between the two\n    83→// persistently thwart achievement).\n    84→//\n    85→// As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n    86→// non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n    87→// removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n    88→// removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n    89→// too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n    90→// problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n    91→//\n    92→// The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n    93→// objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n    94→// Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n    95→// a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n    96→// into its constituent parts.\n    97→//\n    98→// Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n    99→// snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n   100→// will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n   101→//\n   102→// A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\n   103→// update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n   104→// added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n   105→// stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n   106→// after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n   107→// additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n   108→// client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n   109→// local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n   110→// SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n   111→// update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n   112→// update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n   113→// corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\n   114→// and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\n   115→// For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\n   116→// delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\n   117→// object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\n   118→// `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n   119→// that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n   120→// `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n   121→// and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n   122→// created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n   123→// rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n   124→// need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n   125→// field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n   126→// notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n   127→//\n   128→// A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n   129→// is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n   130→// notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n   131→// to something else, for example through a\n   132→// `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n   133→//\n   134→// A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n   135→// state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n   136→// ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\n   137→type SharedInformer interface {\n   138→\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n   139→\t// the shared informer's resync period. An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n// namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n// an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n// SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n// group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n// SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n// applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n//\n// The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n// access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n// An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n// other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n//\n// A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n// by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n// machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n// the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n// consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n// prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n// particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n// then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n// eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n// state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n// service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n// absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n// selector.\n//\n// For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n// states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n// states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n// might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n// states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n// ordering between states seen for different objects.\n//\n// The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n// during `Run()`.\n//\n// As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n// unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n// collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n// SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n// collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n// service ends, or communication problems between the two\n// persistently thwart achievement).\n//\n// As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n// non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n// removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n// removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n// too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n// problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n//\n// The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n// objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n// Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n// a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n// into its constituent parts.\n//\n// Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n// snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n// will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n//\n// A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\n// update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n// added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n// stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n// after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n// additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n// client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n// local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n// SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n// update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n// update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n// corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\n// and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\n// For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\n// delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\n// object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\n// `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n// that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n// `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n// and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n// created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n// rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n// need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n// field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n// notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n//\n// A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n// is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n// notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n// to something else, for example through a\n// `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n//\n// A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n// state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n// ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\ntype SharedInformer interface {\n\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n\t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\n\t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\n\t// different handlers.\n\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\n\t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\n\t// seen every item in the initial list).\n\tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n\t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the\n\t// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means\n\t// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation\n\t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\n\t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1019}}}

called by controller's processLoop\n4. **Controller** (`controller.go`) - `processLoop()` calls `Queue.Pop()` with `Process` function; for sharedIndexInformer this is `HandleDeltas`\n5. **sharedIndexInformer** (`shared_informer.go`) - `HandleDeltas()` calls `processDeltas()` which calls `clientState.Add/Update/Delete` and `handler.OnAdd` to notify registered event handlers\n6. **sharedProcessor.distribute()** - distributes notifications to registered `processorListener`s\n7. **processorListener.pop()** and **processorListener.run()** - relay notifications to the actual entirely in client-go--v0.32.0/tools/cache/ and flows as follows:\\n\\n## 1. ListWatch — tools/cache/listwatch.go\\n\\n`ListWatch` (struct) implements the `ListerWatcher` interface, which combines `Lister` and `Watcher`. `NewListWatchFromClient` and `NewFilteredListWatchFromClient` create a `ListWatch` that makes REST calls to the API server: `ListWatch.List()` does a GET (list) and `ListWatch.Watch()` opens a long-lived HTTP watch stream, both delegated through `ListFunc`/`WatchFunc` closures built against the REST client.\\n\\n## 2. Reflector — tools/cache/reflector.go\\n\\n`Reflector` drives the data flow from the API server into the local store. `Reflector.Run()` calls `ListAndWatch()` in a backoff loop. `ListAndWatch()` either:\\n- Calls `list()` (which uses `listerWatcher.List()` via a pager, then calls `store.Replace()` to seed the DeltaFIFO), or\\n- Calls `watchList()` (streaming WatchList feature, uses `listerWatcher.Watch()` with `SendInitialEvents=true` and calls `store.Replace()` on bookmark receipt).\\n\\nThen it calls `watchWithResync()` → `watch()` → `handleAnyWatch()` (also `handleWatch`/`handleListWatch` are thin wrappers). `handleAnyWatch()` reads watch events from `w.ResultChan()` and calls `store.Add()`, `store.Update()`, or `store.Delete()` on the DeltaFIFO for ADDED/MODIFIED/DELETED events respectively.\\n\\n## 3. DeltaFIFO — tools/cache/delta_fifo.go\\n\\n`DeltaFIFO` is the queue between the Reflector and the processing loop. `Add()`, `Update()`, `Delete()`, and `Replace()` are called by the Reflector and enqueue `Delta` objects (with types Added, Updated, Deleted, Replaced, Sync). `Pop()` dequeues deltas and calls the supplied `PopProcessFunc` (which is `Config.Process`).\\n\\n## 4. Controller / processLoop — tools/cache/controller.go\\n\\n`controller.Run()` creates a `Reflector` (wiring `ListerWatcher` → DeltaFIFO store) and starts it, then runs `processLoop()` in a loop. `processLoop()` calls `Queue.Pop(PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))`. For simple informers (`NewInformer`/`NewIndexerInformer`), `Process` is a closure that calls `processDeltas()`. `processDeltas()` iterates each delta, updates `clientState` (the local Store/Indexer) via `Add`/`Update`/`Delete`, and dispatches to the `ResourceEventHandler` via `handler.OnAdd()`, `handler.OnUpdate()`, or `handler.OnDelete()`.\\n\\n## 5. sharedIndexInformer / HandleDeltas — tools/cache/shared_informer.go\\n\\nFor shared informers (`NewSharedIndexInformer` etc.), `sharedIndexInformer.Run()` constructs the DeltaFIFO and Config with `Process: s.HandleDeltas`. `HandleDeltas()` calls `processDeltas()` with `s` (sharedIndexInformer itself) as the handler and `s.indexer` as the store. The sharedIndexInformer implements `ResourceEventHandler` (`OnAdd`, `OnUpdate`, `OnDelete`), and each of these methods calls `s.processor.distribute()` to fan out to all registered listeners.\\n\\n## 6. sharedProcessor / processorListener dispatch — tools/cache/shared_informer.go\\n\\n`sharedProcessor.distribute()` iterates `p.listeners` (map of `*processorListener` → isSyncing) and calls `listener.add(notification)` for every applicable listener. Each `processorListener` has two goroutines:\\n- `pop()` reads from `addCh` and pumps notifications through a ring buffer to `nextCh`.\\n- `run()` reads from `nextCh` and calls the actual user-registered `ResourceEventHandler` methods: `handler.OnAdd()`, `handler.OnUpdate()`, `handler.OnDelete()`.\\n\\nUsers register handlers via `sharedIndexInformer.AddEventHandler()` / `AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod()`, which creates a `processorListener` wrapping the user's `ResourceEventHandler` and adds it to `sharedProcessor`.\\n\\n## 7. Store / cache / threadSafeMap — tools/cache/store.go, thread_safe_store.go\\n\\nThe local cache (`cache` struct in store.go) wraps a `ThreadSafeStore` (implemented by `threadSafeMap` in thread_safe_store.go). `cache.Add/Update/Delete/Replace` are called during delta processing to keep the in-memory index consistent. The indexer (used by sharedIndexInformer) is the same `cache` with indexers configured.\\n\\n## Summary of the chain\\n\\n```\\nAPI Server watch event\\n  → ListWatch.Watch() / ListWatch.List()          [listwatch.go]\\n  → Reflector.ListAndWatch() / handleAnyWatch()   [reflector.go]\\n  → DeltaFIFO.Add/Update/Delete/Replace           [delta_fifo.go]\\n  → controller.processLoop() → DeltaFIFO.Pop()    [controller.go]\\n  → sharedIndexInformer.HandleDeltas()             [shared_informer.go]\\n  → processDeltas() → clientState.Add/Update/Delete + handler.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete [controller.go]\\n  → sharedIndexInformer.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete   [shared_informer.go]\\n  → sharedProcessor.distribute()                  [shared_informer.go]\\n  → processorListener.add() → pop() → run()       [shared_informer.go]\\n  → user ResourceEventHandler.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete\\n```\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":370,"cache_read_input_tokens":55243,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":370,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":7,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c08fcc2c-4f4b-49df-8dd7-5f31748882d0","uuid":"84ddac06-a529-4a71-9b1e-b62e38c9b55d"}

entirely in client-go--v0.32.0/tools/cache/ and flows as follows:\\n\\n## 1. ListWatch — tools/cache/listwatch.go\\n\\n`ListWatch` (struct) implements the `ListerWatcher` interface, which combines `Lister` and `Watcher`. `NewListWatchFromClient` and `NewFilteredListWatchFromClient` create a `ListWatch` that makes REST calls to the API server: `ListWatch.List()` does a GET (list) and `ListWatch.Watch()` opens a long-lived HTTP watch stream, both delegated through `ListFunc`/`WatchFunc` closures built against the REST client.\\n\\n## 2. Reflector — tools/cache/reflector.go\\n\\n`Reflector` drives the data flow from the API server into the local store. `Reflector.Run()` calls `ListAndWatch()` in a backoff loop. `ListAndWatch()` either:\\n- Calls `list()` (which uses `listerWatcher.List()` via a pager, then calls `store.Replace()` to seed the DeltaFIFO), or\\n- Calls `watchList()` (streaming WatchList feature, uses `listerWatcher.Watch()` with `SendInitialEvents=true` and calls `store.Replace()` on bookmark receipt).\\n\\nThen it calls `watchWithResync()` → `watch()` → `handleAnyWatch()` (also `handleWatch`/`handleListWatch` are thin wrappers). `handleAnyWatch()` reads watch events from `w.ResultChan()` and calls `store.Add()`, `store.Update()`, or `store.Delete()` on the DeltaFIFO for ADDED/MODIFIED/DELETED events respectively.\\n\\n## 3. DeltaFIFO — tools/cache/delta_fifo.go\\n\\n`DeltaFIFO` is the queue between the Reflector and the processing loop. `Add()`, `Update()`, `Delete()`, and `Replace()` are called by the Reflector and enqueue `Delta` objects (with types Added, Updated, Deleted, Replaced, Sync). `Pop()` dequeues deltas and calls the supplied `PopProcessFunc` (which is `Config.Process`).\\n\\n## 4. Controller / processLoop — tools/cache/controller.go\\n\\n`controller.Run()` creates a `Reflector` (wiring `ListerWatcher` → DeltaFIFO store) and starts it, then runs `processLoop()` in a loop. `processLoop()` calls `Queue.Pop(PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))`. For simple informers (`NewInformer`/`NewIndexerInformer`), `Process` is a closure that calls `processDeltas()`. `processDeltas()` iterates each delta, updates `clientState` (the local Store/Indexer) via `Add`/`Update`/`Delete`, and dispatches to the `ResourceEventHandler` via `handler.OnAdd()`, `handler.OnUpdate()`, or `handler.OnDelete()`.\\n\\n## 5. sharedIndexInformer / HandleDeltas — tools/cache/shared_informer.go\\n\\nFor shared informers (`NewSharedIndexInformer` etc.), `sharedIndexInformer.Run()` constructs the DeltaFIFO and Config with `Process: s.HandleDeltas`. `HandleDeltas()` calls `processDeltas()` with `s` (sharedIndexInformer itself) as the handler and `s.indexer` as the store. The sharedIndexInformer implements `ResourceEventHandler` (`OnAdd`, `OnUpdate`, `OnDelete`), and each of these methods calls `s.processor.distribute()` to fan out to all registered listeners.\\n\\n## 6. sharedProcessor / processorListener dispatch — tools/cache/shared_informer.go\\n\\n`sharedProcessor.distribute()` iterates `p.listeners` (map of `*processorListener` → isSyncing) and calls `listener.add(notification)` for every applicable listener. Each `processorListener` has two goroutines:\\n- `pop()` reads from `addCh` and pumps notifications through a ring buffer to `nextCh`.\\n- `run()` reads from `nextCh` and calls the actual user-registered `ResourceEventHandler` methods: `handler.OnAdd()`, `handler.OnUpdate()`, `handler.OnDelete()`.\\n\\nUsers register handlers via `sharedIndexInformer.AddEventHandler()` / `AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod()`, which creates a `processorListener` wrapping the user's `ResourceEventHandler` and adds it to `sharedProcessor`.\\n\\n## 7. Store / cache / threadSafeMap — tools/cache/store.go, thread_safe_store.go\\n\\nThe local cache (`cache` struct in store.go) wraps a `ThreadSafeStore` (implemented by `threadSafeMap` in thread_safe_store.go). `cache.Add/Update/Delete/Replace` are called during delta processing to keep the in-memory index consistent. The indexer (used by sharedIndexInformer) is the same `cache` with indexers configured.\\n\\n## Summary of the chain\\n\\n```\\nAPI Server watch event\\n  → ListWatch.Watch() / ListWatch.List()          [listwatch.go]\\n  → Reflector.ListAndWatch() / handleAnyWatch()   [reflector.go]\\n  → DeltaFIFO.Add/Update/Delete/Replace           [delta_fifo.go]\\n  → controller.processLoop() → DeltaFIFO.Pop()    [controller.go]\\n  → sharedIndexInformer.HandleDeltas()             [shared_informer.go]\\n  → processDeltas() → clientState.Add/Update/Delete + handler.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete [controller.go]\\n  → sharedIndexInformer.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete   [shared_informer.go]\\n  → sharedProcessor.distribute()                  [shared_informer.go]\\n  → processorListener.add() → pop() → run()       [shared_informer.go]\\n  → user ResourceEventHandler.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete\\n```\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
